<span id="freeTextContainer7321093303436701365">They were the Sheridan men, ruled by passion, betrayed by love, heirs to a legacy of violence and forbidden desire.Gus, Boston's top homicide cop: he knew equally well the backroom politics of City Hall and the private passions of the very rich, a man haunted by the wanton courage and perilous obsessions he inherited from his father... Conn, the patriarch, a lawless cop wh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7321093303436701365">They were the Sheridan men, ruled by passion, betrayed by love, heirs to a legacy of violence and forbidden desire.  Gus, Boston's top homicide cop: he knew equally well the backroom politics of City Hall and the private passions of the very rich, a man haunted by the wanton courage and perilous obsessions he inherited from his father... Conn, the patriarch, a lawless cop who spawned a circle of vengeance and betrayal that would span half a century... and Chris, Gus's beloved son, a Harvard lawyer and criminologist, fated to risk everything to break the chain of obsession and rage...  Three generations linked by crime and punishment--cops and heroes, fathers, sons, and lovers united at last by revelations that could bring a family to its knees...<br /><br /><br /><em>From the Paperback edition.</em></span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_26107598">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26107598" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="left imgcol" title="Kemper"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451574879p2/405390.jpg" alt="Kemper" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26107598?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/405390-kemper" class="user" title="Kemper">Kemper</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1430637.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="Hardcover 9780385304375" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery" class="actionLinkLite">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2012-reread" class="actionLinkLite">2012-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26107598">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14154419099136742997">I read an interview with Robert B. Parker in which he said that he thought <em>All Our Yesterdays</em> was probably his best book, but that it was also one of his worst selling ones. It was certainly among his most ambitious and came just before his Spenser books started a serious decline in quality.<br /><br />Would RBP have taken on some bigger challenges and not allowed Spenser to grow repetitive and stale if this would have been more successful? He created three new series as well as doing some other stand-alone</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14154419099136742997">I read an interview with Robert B. Parker in which he said that he thought <em>All Our Yesterdays</em> was probably his best book, but that it was also one of his worst selling ones. It was certainly among his most ambitious and came just before his Spenser books started a serious decline in quality.<br /><br />Would RBP have taken on some bigger challenges and not allowed Spenser to grow repetitive and stale if this would have been more successful? He created three new series as well as doing some other stand-alone novels after this was published so it’s not like he just quit trying new things, but it does seem like the last time he’d do something really outside his normal comfort zone. <br /><br />Conn Sheridan is a soldier in the Irish Republican Army in 1920 when he meets Hadley Winslow, the beautiful wife of a rich American visiting Dublin. The two have a passionate affair, and Conn eventually asks Hadley to leave her husband. She refuses, things get ugly, and Conn has to flee to Boston.<br /><br />In America, Conn joins the police, but the heartbreak of losing Hadley has left him not giving much of a shit about anything. Years pass, and he marries a woman he doesn’t love after getting her pregnant. While he feels some attachment to his son Gus, he’s still unable to get emotionally involved in anything until he discovers something that allows him to blackmail Hadley into resuming their affair.<br /><br />More time passes. Gus eventually joins the police, too, and he also learns the Winslow secret. Gus gets trapped in another loveless marriage but is completely devoted to his own son, Chris. Chris eventually falls in love with the granddaughter of Hadley, but they’re unaware that their families have a long history of obsessive love and blackmail. A mid-90s Boston gang war starts a chain of events that threatens to expose the past.<br /><br />RBP used a lot of his favorite themes here. There’s the ‘good’ man who is completely in love with a ‘bad’ woman, and there’s also a woman who has to cheat on her lover to ultimately prove to herself that their love is real. Father and son relationships play a big part of it, too. There’s also a couple of completely useless and overbearing mother figures in the story which is another RBP favorite. (Between his repeated character of the stupid, drunken, overbearing mother in several books and Spenser’s origin story of being raised by his father and two uncles after his mother died in childbirth, I’ve got a hunch that RBP may have had more than a few mommy issues.)<br /><br />What sets this one apart is that RBP didn’t just forgive his characters for their behavior and allow them to be heroic anyhow. Conn’s inability to let Hadley go cuts him off from anyone else he should care about, including his son, and also causes him to do some fairly unsavory shit. Gus’s refusal to leave a wife he doesn’t love because of his devotion to young Chris leaves him coasting unhappily through life and leads him to follow Conn‘s example of cutting corners. Adult Chris’s love of Grace is obsessive to the point of suffocating her and is killing their relationship. Usually, RBP portrayed the men who refuse to give up on their love for someone no matter what happens as romantic and admirable. Here, he more accurately portrays it as unhealthy and something that will seriously screw up your life.<br /><br />In a perfect world, this would have been the culmination of the theme of obsessive love for RBP, and he would have moved on to other things after getting it all out of his system in this book. Unfortunately, like one of his own characters, RBP could never let it go and would continue to make it one of the main characteristics of most of his work for the rest of his life. Still, this book about three generations of men suffering because of their hang-ups was some of his best writing on the subject.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14154419099136742997">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_256232785">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/256232785" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2231715-lewis-weinstein" class="left imgcol" title="Lewis Weinstein"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442501879p2/2231715.jpg" alt="Lewis Weinstein" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/256232785?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 21, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2231715-lewis-weinstein" class="user" title="Lewis Weinstein">Lewis Weinstein</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1430637.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="Hardcover 9780385304375" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2231715-lewis-weinstein?shelf=crime-and-thrillers" class="actionLinkLite">crime-and-thrillers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer256232785">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1092108654224471853">This is really an extraordinary book. I expected a typical non-memorable crime/thriller story, of which I read many. Instead, here is a brilliantly constructed multi-generational exploration of the very interesting lives of some very flawed people. And does Parker ever make me care about these people!<br /><br />There was something unusual and very powerful about the structure of the story. It reached what seemed to me could have been the conclusion of a shorter novel about half-way through, at a point when</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1092108654224471853">This is really an extraordinary book. I expected a typical non-memorable crime/thriller story, of which I read many. Instead, here is a brilliantly constructed multi-generational exploration of the very interesting lives of some very flawed people. And does Parker ever make me care about these people!<br /><br />There was something unusual and very powerful about the structure of the story. It reached what seemed to me could have been the conclusion of a shorter novel about half-way through, at a point when many novels are struggling with that fearsome middle-of-the-book trough. (Since I was reading the book on kindle, I didn't know how far along I was and thought the story was about to end. When I checked, I learned I was at 48%.) But exactly here Parker gathers up a new burst of writing energy and the story takes off again, with one revelation after another, until the final resolution many worthwhile reading hours away.<br /><br />Parker's use of time is also worthy of note, especially for me since he does so successfully what I am struggling to achieve in my own novel-in-progress. You start in the present in Boston, with two people who seem to love each other but are not clear if they can be together. Some cataclysmic event has thrown them into relationship disarray. Then you jump back 70 years, and a young man in Dublin is an IRA terrorist fighting British domination in Ireland. The story emerges in a series of flashbacks, and in the very skillful and emotional revelation of the impact of these past events on the original two lovers, getting ever closer to the present. To say more would reveal too much.<br /><br />Parker has of course been enormously successful, although I have read only 1-2 of his subsequent crime stories, which I do not remember. Another Goodreads reviewer said Parker never again reached the level of excellence of this early novel that did not have much commercial success. If that is true, what a shame that he was not encouraged to reach harder for the literary excellence that was clearly within his potential.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1092108654224471853">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_44586805">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44586805" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w" class="left imgcol" title="Eric_W"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1429386336p2/1711431.jpg" alt="Eric_W" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/44586805?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1711431-eric-w" class="user" title="Eric_W">Eric_W</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/414467.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="Paperback 9780440221463" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1711431-eric-w?shelf=police-procedural" class="actionLinkLite">police-procedural</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer44586805">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18157282772725735831">Surprise, surprise, a Robert Parker that does not feature Hawk or Spencer and does not even have a private detective. I think this is one of his best yet. Spanning three generations it follows the men of the Sheridan family, greatly flawed, who seek to redeem themselves of an obsession for violence and corruption that becomes a hex. Their lives all become entwined with the Winslows, to the detriment of all.<br /> Conn Sheridan, the patriarch, is a young sniper for the IRA. He is assigned the assassina</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18157282772725735831">Surprise, surprise, a Robert Parker that does not feature Hawk or Spencer and does not even have a private detective. I think this is one of his best yet. Spanning three generations it follows the men of the Sheridan family, greatly flawed, who seek to redeem themselves of an obsession for violence and corruption that becomes a hex. Their lives all become entwined with the Winslows, to the detriment of all.<br />	Conn Sheridan, the patriarch, is a young sniper for the IRA. He is assigned the assassination of an English politician. After being sold out by Hadley Winslow, his married lover, he escapes from British prison just before he is to be shot, and leaves for America. He becomes a cop, a rather corrupt one at that, whose son Gus inherits, or assumes, that corruptness but doesn't want it to singe his son Chris. <br />	The story is told through a variety of perspectives, starting with conversations between Chris and his girlfriend Grace, the daughter of Tom Winslow, Hadley's son. Tom has a nsty secret. As a teenager, he had raped and killed a young girl, a crime that was covered up by Conn, who used the information to blackmail Hadley into resuming their affair. Conn passed along evidence of Tom's pedophilia – Tom had been sent to a private clinic in Switzerland as part of the deal with Hadley to hush up the murder – to Gus, who continued to use it as a hold over Tom, now returned from his Swiss hiatus and manager of a large bank. Gus has also been on the take from two Irish crime families and is using Tom's bank to launder their ill-gotten gains. <br />	It all comes crashing down when one of the henchmen of the crime families is gunned down and an innocent school girl is killed in the cross-fire. Gus's soon, Chris, is appointed by the mayor, Parnell Flaherty, a candidate for the Senate seat also sought by Cabot Winslow, Grace's sister (it does get rather intertwined,) as special prosecutor to end the crime war between the two families. Gus, realizing that the only way he can help his son succeed is by revealing everything, warns the crime bosses that he is changing sides. This pressures Tom into killing two more young girls and the Sheridans and Winslows are soon revealed to be mired in corruption. Only Chris and Grace appear to have achieved some form of salvation through the efforts of Gus and Laura, Grace's mother, who realize that only through their sacrifice can the two children escape the insidious effects of bad marriages and corruption their families have become mired in.<br />	It all sounds a bit coincidental and too intertwined, but Parker has skillfully woven a story that cannot be put down. <br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18157282772725735831">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_938932394">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/938932394" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6637209-cathy-dupont" class="left imgcol" title="Cathy DuPont"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1393680963p2/6637209.jpg" alt="Cathy DuPont" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/938932394?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2014</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17394019854803566163">I've read so many RBP books, mostly the Spenser series, and I want and need to read Parker's books faster to get them off my shelf. (The shelf is sinking!) <br /><br />Chose this one because it wasn't a Spenser and looked pretty interesting. Wish I could say it was. <br /><br />RBP said he thought it was his best book written but I surely don't agree. <em>The Godwulf Manuscript</em> still resonates with me, the first in the Spenser series. <br /><br />As I was reading <em>All Our Yesterdays</em> it occurred to me that Parker probably thought he was</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17394019854803566163">I've read so many RBP books, mostly the Spenser series, and I want and need to read Parker's books faster to get them off my shelf. (The shelf is sinking!) <br /><br />Chose this one because it wasn't a Spenser and looked pretty interesting. Wish I could say it was. <br /><br />RBP said he thought it was his best book written but I surely don't agree. <em>The Godwulf Manuscript</em> still resonates with me, the first in the Spenser series. <br /><br />As I was reading <em>All Our Yesterdays</em> it occurred to me that Parker probably thought he was writing the Best American Novel of the 20th Century. But no, not even close and I really love Parker. <br /><br />I read the description written with the book and that really says it all; it's full of what I think is contrived drama, links to family members that scream concocted, romance scenes that seem awkward and with forced descriptions and so on and so forth. (Well, one romance does seem sincere.)<br /><br />The only thing that rang true was graft by Boston cops. I would say that graft was rampant in all big cities and probably most smaller cities in the 1920's, '30's and 1940's and who knows when it petered out, if it did. <br /><br />I love Robert B. Parker. This book was ok but not his best effort, IMO. Sorry, Mr. Parker. RIP. </span>

      <a href="/user/show/8013632-izzy" class="user" title="Izzy">Izzy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1095513921">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3994299880185463095">All Our Yesterdays chronicles three generations of an Irish-American family in Boston. It all starts with Conn, a fighter in the IRA during the Troubles in 1920's Ireland where he falls for a marries American woman named Hadley. Conn's passion and Obsession for Hadley has him crossing the river to Boston where he becomes a crooked cop and finds himself with a family. He has a son named Gus who goes to Korea and becomes a cop when he returns. He goes as far as becoming the Commander of the Homici</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3994299880185463095">All Our Yesterdays chronicles three generations of an Irish-American family in Boston. It all starts with Conn, a fighter in the IRA during the Troubles in 1920's Ireland where he falls for a marries American woman named Hadley. Conn's passion and Obsession for Hadley has him crossing the river to Boston where he becomes a crooked cop and finds himself with a family. He has a son named Gus who goes to Korea and becomes a cop when he returns. He goes as far as becoming the Commander of the Homicide Unit. That position has him blackmailing the wealthy as well as taking bribes from warring mobsters whose gangland killings catch the attention of the Mayor's office. Then there is Chris, a Harvard Law Criminologist who is appointed as the Special Prosecutor brought in to end this gang war everyone involved in city politics knows about but are only now starting to take seriously.<br />This story is an opera much like Mystic River in a way. It is a tale of three generations of two families and their involvement with violence, passions, obsession, lust, greed, crime, family and ultimately love. It is about cops and robbers, lovers and fighters &amp; parents and their children. I recommend this book to anyone who wants to read a meaningful and exciting drama with just a hint of action.</span>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer988949577">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6634430245140566859">I've read ALL of Robert B. Parker's books, except for a couple I can't find, since March 18, 2013. "All Our Yesterdays" stands alone as the best of the bunch, totally apart from, and far above, the others in excellence. There is no hint of the Spenser, Hawk, Susan, Jesse, Sunny, Virgil, or Everett characters. We become totally wrapped up in the psychological varieties of Conn, Gus, Chris, Hadley, Grace, and Laura. We sorrow in the predestined travails of Tom, who we continue to see and read abou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6634430245140566859">I've read ALL of Robert B. Parker's books, except for a couple I can't find, since March 18, 2013. "All Our Yesterdays" stands alone as the best of the bunch, totally apart from, and far above, the others in excellence. There is no hint of the Spenser, Hawk, Susan, Jesse, Sunny, Virgil, or Everett characters. We become totally wrapped up in the psychological varieties of Conn, Gus, Chris, Hadley, Grace, and Laura. We sorrow in the predestined travails of Tom, who we continue to see and read about in the daily news. Even with the distinct characterizations, I hope Parker's women are not typical of real life. In a perfect world, all the men would be like Chris, I hope. I am moving on to more crime and generational fiction, but I'm grateful for this side trip into "All Our Yesterdays". And, what a fascinating trip it was! </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer921912426">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3909121450875533598">I'm not at all sure what to make of All Our Yesterdays. Only rarely did I get a glimmer of the Robert B. Parker that I've come to know and love. I read somewhere that he considered this one of his better efforts. Perhaps he was trying to be a more "serious" writer. I think he was pretty serious in the niche that he filled so well for so many years - a good story, told with wit, that can be read in an evening and save one from having to stare at the drivel on the tube. I am wondering what I would</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3909121450875533598">I'm not at all sure what to make of All Our Yesterdays. Only rarely did I get a glimmer of the Robert B. Parker that I've come to know and love. I read somewhere that he considered this one of his better efforts. Perhaps he was trying to be a more "serious" writer. I think he was pretty serious in the niche that he filled so well for so many years - a good story, told with wit, that can be read in an evening and save one from having to stare at the drivel on the tube. I am wondering what I would have thought of the book had it not been written by Parker? There wasn't a single character in this book that I could identify with at all - in his Spencer books, I even like the bad guys some of the time. I'm glad he got back to doing what he did best.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11259182894317133386">There is nothing better than a good Irish cop story set in Boston. There is corruption, womanizing, some murders, mob boss crap, all mixed together to tell the story about 3 generations of an immigrant Irish family who hold the tradition of law enforcement. Even if this isn't your "cup o' tea" read the book. It is well detailed, reads quickly, and like every really good book, leaves you wanting more even though the story wraps up nicely. <br /><br />If you got a pair, it means this book is for you!<br /><br />That is u</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11259182894317133386">There is nothing better than a good Irish cop story set in Boston. There is corruption, womanizing, some murders, mob boss crap, all mixed together to tell the story about 3 generations of an immigrant Irish family who hold the tradition of law enforcement. Even if this isn't your "cup o' tea" read the book. It is well detailed, reads quickly, and like every really good book, leaves you wanting more even though the story wraps up nicely. <br /><br />If you got a pair, it means this book is for you!<br /><br />That is unless you'd rather some of those dime-store, "I'm a 20 something year old female" books that seem to clog the bookshelves right now. Ack! If I see another "I'm a strong independent girl, who sleeps around casually with no repercussions in search for love and have no idea about a damned thing in life" books I'm packing it in. If that is what women really find entertaining I may as well just start playing Playstation all day long, rubbing myself with cream cheese and find my dates with an overweight girl on the internet! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11259182894317133386">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6310998847682692946">3 generations of Irish men are intertwined...<br /><br />Conn - 1920s - IRA soldier/soldier mentality... injured, falls in love with Hadley, a married American volunteer who will have sex with him but will not leave her rich husband for him.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText6310998847682692946">3 generations of Irish men are intertwined...<br /><br />Conn - 1920s - IRA soldier/soldier mentality... injured, falls in love with Hadley, a married American volunteer who will have sex with him but will not leave her rich husband for him. She turns him into the British, he escapes to Boston before executed &amp; becomes a cop. He is emotionally cold &amp; cut off, uncaring... he marries one of the gals he got pregnant - who punishes them all with her religious guilt for the rest of their lives... he loves his son Gus as best he can, but he is indifferent most of the time. His married love's son is a pediphile who ends up raping &amp; murdering a 9 year old girl... as the investigating cop he sees his love for the 1st time in 20 years, and she is still beautiful... he makes an agreement that if the son is sent to Switzerland for treatment, and she meets him once a week, for sex and money, he will not arrest her son... he ends his life by walking into a bullet that could have been avoided.<br /><br />Gus.... becomes a cop... he marries unwisely, a selfcentered, childlike woman who cannot deal with the stresses of life - especially child rearing...continues with the grift of his father, and especially with Hadley as his father left the evidence for him and he needs the money... he loves his son and tries to make up for his wife's shortcomings as much as possible. <br /><br />Chris is the one telling the story... he loves Hadley's granddaughter Grace, but too obsessively. He tells her the family story to show her he has grown and is ready to love her wisely...<br /><br />Chris is unlike his father &amp; grandfather in that he is academic / intellectual... and has a degree in criminology but no practical experience.<br /><br />Gus is chief of detectives - and taking money from the two main crime bosses in Boston... and a turf war has started. The mayor is running for senate, and decides to appoint Chris as special prosecuter to investigate &amp; stop the turf war. Gus does what he needs to do to make his son a success - which ends up meaning turning himself in as states evidence against the crime bosses... when he confesses all to Chris, Chris does right by his father and by the city...<br /><br />And Grace agrees to marry him... Chris is the first one in 3 generations to find the right woman, and to be the right man.<br /><br /></span>

      <a href="/user/show/329996-david" class="user" title="David">David</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/329996-david?shelf=mysteries" class="actionLinkLite">mysteries</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/329996-david?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer169201281">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3460055347309878089"><u>All Our Yesterdays</u>by Robert B. Parker (Delacourte Press 1994)(Fiction - Mystery) is not the typical RBP novel. One glaring difference is that <u>All Our Yesterdays</u> is a stand-alone novel of 401 pages rather that being part of one of the author's several popular series, usually featuring a familiar protagonist/hero. I tried and failed to make it through this book in the past. I've twice in the past read the first fifty-or-so pages without engaging, but this time I kept just enough momentum going to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3460055347309878089"><u>All Our Yesterdays</u> by Robert B. Parker (Delacourte Press 1994)(Fiction - Mystery) is not the typical RBP novel. One glaring difference is that <u>All Our Yesterdays</u> is a stand-alone novel of 401 pages rather that being part of one of the author's several popular series, usually featuring a familiar protagonist/hero. I tried and failed to make it through this book in the past. I've twice in the past read the first fifty-or-so pages without engaging, but this time I kept just enough momentum going to stay on the crest and finish the thing. Was it great? I don't think so. Would I recommend it? Not unless the reader hadn't read all of the Tombstone series with Virgil and Everett and had not yet read his or her own personal fill of Spencer/Jesse Stone/Sunny Randall novels. Heck, the only reason that I read this one was that I stumbled upon Parker's website. I was stunned to know that he is dead lo these past few years and that he considers this novel, <u>All Our Yesterdays</u>, to be his favorite/his best. For that reason, I tried to read it for the third time and finally succeeded. My rating: 7/10 (he gets a free point bonus for being who he is), finished 5/18/11.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3460055347309878089">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2617610160728482328">This Parker book has elements of all of his novels, but it is also very different. Lots of human pathos is examined and dissected, all with an extremely spare and elegant prose. I always have to marvel at how much Parker can say with just a few words. One of my favorite sentences: "The silence explored the room slowly and filled it the way water rises in a bucket." This comes at a pivotal moment in the storyline and a very sad one as well.<br /><br />It is not an easy read, as the story revolves not only ar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2617610160728482328">This Parker book has elements of all of his novels, but it is also very different. Lots of human pathos is examined and dissected, all with an extremely spare and elegant prose. I always have to marvel at how much Parker can say with just a few words. One of my favorite sentences: "The silence explored the room slowly and filled it the way water rises in a bucket." This comes at a pivotal moment in the storyline and a very sad one as well.<br /><br />It is not an easy read, as the story revolves not only around family of origin issues, Irish history, and the general frailty of human nature, but the evil of pedophilia. It's difficult to read the sections where the pedophile is setting up and committing his crimes, as Parker pulls no punches.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15650337478423846192"> O.K. Now I've read all that Robert B. Parker, has written. I've also read that the Spenser and Stone stories will continue to be written and published. In the last Jesse Stone novel "Night and Day" Jesse's relationship with Sunny Randal has brought her and Spike to Paradise.<br /> All Our Yesterdays is a story that shows Parker's love of Boston and all things Irish not to mention an appearance of his favorite German short hairs. The Story itself was written with a depth of emotion and a story that ha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15650337478423846192"> O.K. Now I've read all that Robert B. Parker, has written. I've also read that the Spenser and Stone stories will continue to be written and published. In the last Jesse Stone novel "Night and Day" Jesse's relationship with Sunny Randal has brought her and Spike to Paradise.<br /> All Our Yesterdays is a story that shows Parker's love of Boston and all things Irish not to mention an appearance of his favorite German short hairs. The Story itself was written with a depth of emotion and a story that had my attention from the beginning. Three generations of family interaction are resolved in one of DR. Parker's best books.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_48687231">

  <a href="/user/show/1882431-joy" class="left imgcol" title="Joy"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Joy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48687231?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 09, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1882431-joy" class="user" title="Joy">Joy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/414467.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="Paperback 9780440221463" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48687231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9210114453541521690">This was the first Parker book I read that wasn't about Spenser,<br />Jesse Stone, or Sunny Randall. In fact, I kept moving it to the<br />bottom of the pile for that reason. It turned out to be the best<br />of all books on character development--three generations of Sheridan<br />men who were "ruled by passion, betrayed by love." The sins of the<br />fathers were really passsed on to the sons, but by the third<br />generation, the son really breaks the 'stronghold.' It was almost<br />a story of redemption.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_188128437">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/188128437" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5861360-bruce-snell" class="left imgcol" title="Bruce Snell"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311443834p2/5861360.jpg" alt="Bruce Snell" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/188128437?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 23, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5861360-bruce-snell" class="user" title="Bruce Snell">Bruce Snell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/414467.All_Our_Yesterdays" title="Paperback 9780440221463" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer188128437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2201066859579708709">This might be the best book Parker wrote in his long career. It would have been better if he had left out the sections about Chris's problems with his love life, but all in all, the rest of the story was good enough to make up for that shortcoming. The story was about 3 generations of Irish Boston cops, and I think the first generation (Con) was good enough that it could have been a book all by itself. The ending was a bit obvious, but it was fun getting there.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/4850019-debi?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer13231969456146383857">Really, a very good read. Parker writes in the way that I tend to think. He sees the antecedents for current actions in the lives of our grandparents. Because s/he did this, I did that. His timing is impecable, his plot intellectual and emotional and his ending totally unforeseen. Bravo.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oc3MdmujkV3eip3MGpcOWKYbHiO8RW0dQwsxD9RrC7zEGfOlmXGFp1JS6Xdk9ujq7+zdOvWYKrcpAjSdGP79+Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('48sYup6AwN/4kWWIpuxY3oJ3L55ywmYQQcOzLVQoNM6GHydpbFLUJXRJETPYjb5sy4DshzsfIboryra/mL3Ciw==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/397.Robert_B_Parker">About Robert B. Parker</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/397.Robert_B_Parker"><img alt="397" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1423098317p2/397.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer14925694439809489403"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database named <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/similar_names/397">Robert B. Parker</a>.</em><br /><strong>Robert Brown Parker</strong> was an American crime writer. His most famous works were the novels about the private detective Spenser. ABC television network developed the television series <em>Spenser: For Hire</em> based on the character in the late 1980s; a series of TV movies based on the character were also produced.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14925694439809489403"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database named <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/similar_names/397">Robert B. Parker</a>.</em><br /><strong>Robert Brown Parker</strong> was an American crime writer. His most famous works were the novels about the private detective Spenser. ABC television network developed the television series <em>Spenser: For Hire</em> based on the character in the late 1980s; a series of TV movies based on the character were also produced. His works incorporate encyclopedic knowledge of the Boston metropolitan area. Parker was 77 when he died of a heart attack at his home in Cambridge, Massachusetts; discovered at his desk by his wife Joan, he had been working on a novel. The Spenser novels have been cited by critics and bestselling authors such as <a title="Robert Crais" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8944.Robert_Crais">Robert Crais</a>, <a title="Harlan Coben" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/24689.Harlan_Coben">Harlan Coben</a> and <a title="Dennis Lehane" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/21686.Dennis_Lehane">Dennis Lehane</a> as not only influencing their own work but reviving and changing the detective genre.<br />Robert B. Parker was one of contemporary fiction's most popular and respected detective writers. Best known for his portrayal of the tough but erudite investigator Spenser, Parker wrote over twenty-five novels over the course of his career, which began in 1973. Parker's acclaim and his thorough background in classic detective literature helped earn him the somewhat unusual commission of completing a Philip Marlowe novel that the great Raymond Chandler had left unfinished. <br /><br />Promised Land and the other Spenser novels spawned the movie Spenser: For Hire and a string of made-for-TV movies. <br /><br />SERIES DESCRIPTIONS <br /><br />From classic book to classic film, RosettaBooks has gathered some of most memorable books into film available. The selection is broad ranging and far reaching, with books from classic genre to cult classic to science fiction and horror and a blend of the two creating whole new genres like Richard Matheson's The Shrinking Man. Classic works from Vonnegut, one of the greatest writers of the twentieth century, meet with E.M. Forster’s A Passage to India. Whether the work is centered in the here and now, in the past, or in some distant and almost unimaginable future, each work is lasting and memorable and award-winning.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14925694439809489403">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/397.Robert_B_Parker" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Robert B. Parker...</a>

    <div data-current-user-id="false" data-use-wtr-tooltip="true" class="js-dataTooltip">
        <div data-placement="bottom-left" data-resource-id="425174" data-resource-type="Book" class="js-tooltipTrigger tooltipTrigger">
          <a href="/book/show/425174.The_Godwulf_Manuscript"><img width="50" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/books/1420794569m/425174.jpg" id="more_book_425174" /></a>
        </div>
